  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_12fc6753-0d2b-49bb-8d11-aa39fdbaf25f'

<span id="freeTextContainer7019068751009345547">Miryem is the daughter and granddaughter of moneylenders, but her father's inability to collect his debts has left his family on the edge of poverty--until Miryem takes matters into her own hands. Hardening her heart, the young woman sets out to claim what is owed and soon gains a reputation for being able to turn silver into gold. <br/><br/>When an ill-advised boast draws the atten</span>
  <span id="freeText7019068751009345547" style="display:none">Miryem is the daughter and granddaughter of moneylenders, but her father's inability to collect his debts has left his family on the edge of poverty--until Miryem takes matters into her own hands. Hardening her heart, the young woman sets out to claim what is owed and soon gains a reputation for being able to turn silver into gold. <br /><br />When an ill-advised boast draws the attention of the king of the Staryk--grim fey creatures who seem more ice than flesh--Miryem's fate, and that of two kingdoms, will be forever altered. Set an impossible challenge by the nameless king, Miryem unwittingly spins a web that draws in a peasant girl, Wanda, and the unhappy daughter of a local lord who plots to wed his child to the dashing young tsar. <br /><br />But Tsar Mirnatius is not what he seems. And the secret he hides threatens to consume the lands of humans and Staryk alike. Torn between deadly choices, Miryem and her two unlikely allies embark on a desperate quest that will take them to the limits of sacrifice, power, and love. <br /><br />Channeling the vibrant heart of myth and fairy tale, <i>Spinning Silver</i> weaves a multilayered, magical tapestry that readers will want to return to again and again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7019068751009345547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/83857450-bea-honeywell"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/83857450-bea-honeywell">Bea Honeywell</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I follow Naomi on twitter. While I was at Phoenix Comic-Fest, she posted that free copies were being given away at the Del Ray booth and you could get<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I follow Naomi on twitter. While I was at Phoenix Comic-Fest, she posted that free copies were being given away at the Del Ray booth and you could get one if you mentioned the tweet. I followed the instructions to the letter, telling the nice lady manning booth the secret code. She gave me a wink, then ducked under the table and pulled out a Not-For-Sale, For-Promotional-Use-Only, Do-Not-Publish-Quotes, This-Is-Not-Final copy. <br /><br />Follow Naomi on twitter and watch out for giveaways. I happened to be at the right place at the right time. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_590').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div id="review_2428015551" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2428015551" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2428015551?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2018-releases">2018-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2428015551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer484410138722789255">I am officially giving up on having a career to sit on warm patches of moss in the moors and recite bad poetry about how amazing this book is.<br/><br/><strong>I love this book so much</strong>—the kind of love that is peculiar to inhabiting the perspective of young women with agency and the relationships they form when relying on each other. I feel like I should have experienced this novel in some beautiful rose garden under the stars on the biggest bed with silk sheets, laughing maniacally as I burn letters from ex-love</span>
  <span id="freeText484410138722789255" style="display:none">I am officially giving up on having a career to sit on warm patches of moss in the moors and recite bad poetry about how amazing this book is.<br /><br /><strong>I love this book so much</strong>—the kind of love that is peculiar to inhabiting the perspective of young women with agency and the relationships they form when relying on each other. I feel like I should have experienced this novel in some beautiful rose garden under the stars on the biggest bed with silk sheets, laughing maniacally as I burn letters from ex-lovers and eat green tea ice cream with a tiny spoon. It was that <em>iconic</em>.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>So, what's this book about?</u>
</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“So the fairy silver brought you a monster of fire for a husband, and me a monster of ice. We should put them in a room together and let them make us both widows.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><em>Spinning Silver</em> is a brilliant subversive take on the fairytale of <em>Rumpelstiltskin</em> cobbled together with elements of Eastern European folklore and uniquely entwining glistening strands of magic, myth and mystery. Deftly woven into the fabric of this story are the lives of three young women: <strong>Miryem</strong> and <strong>Irina</strong> whose fates seem sealed to a stifled existence and a loveless marriage, and <strong>Wanda</strong> to likely the same, but with a good deal more damage from her father done to her along the way. Their lives become intertwined by fate, their weariness of the men who tried to force their heart somewhere it didn’t belong and of thinking themselves odd because it didn’t fit there, and their desire to settle into something perfect, without jagged corners to catch themselves on.<br /><br /><strong>Miryem</strong> is the daughter of a Jewish moneylender and whose anger and hurt at the gentile townspeople’s mistreatment of her family fused into something cold and unflinching and sharpened into an acumen for quick, high-yield investments. This draws the avaricious attention of the ice-hearted king of the Staryk who promises to make her his queen if she succeeds in turning his Staryk silver into gold three times over and turn her into ice if she fails. Once Miryem is brought to the Staryk’s world, her ability to spin silver into gold manifests itself in the form of actual intrinsic magic and while she’s trapped filling the Staryk's treasure-chests with the gold they yearned for with so much greed, Miryem must also find a way to break the sorcerous winter before her own world fades away forever.<br /><br /><strong>Irina</strong> is the daughter of a duke who sought to sand down her edges and mold her into his own desires, pouring out money by the bucketful to her dowry so she would be wife to whoever made him the best offer. She finds herself marrying none other than the tsar himself—the too-pretty son of a condemned witch whose crown was bought by demon-borrowed magic, an evil thing of smoke and hunger that Irina must find outwit every day just to live.<br /><br /><strong>Wanda</strong> whose house was a place so direly poor that they ran out of food before they ran out of winter, and whose life is drained to the dregs then put down empty by a father who drunk away their borrowed coin until Miryem stood in their half-frozen doorway laying claim to what’s owed to her family. Finding none, she arranges for Wanda to work as a housekeeper for a four-year stint until she pays off the debt. Wanda finds in the company of Miryem’s family a warm and loving haven, away from her violent father and his flaring temper, and quickly becomes a vital member of the family.<br /><br />The stories of these three young women gradually begin to converge and languidly unfold into a gripping and beautifully rendered tale that resonated to my core. I relished every page of this book from first to last. I was hooked, rapturous, wandering through the haze like I have been transported into a fantastical dream. The setting is an enchanting blend of beauty and danger, rendered in languorous and sensuous language. Split between Miryem, Wanda, Irina and then again among other narrators, the leisurely plot flows smoothly and elegantly, weaving all separate threads together with a sure hand, doling out twists and eventually building to a satisfying conclusion.<br /><br /><strong>But it’s the craftly-conceived and fully realized characters that won me over.</strong> Twining themes of agency and the duality of human nature, this book succeeds in creating refreshingly human and real protagonists and anti-heroes. These characters are both strong and deeply flawed, and they—even more strikingly—embrace those qualities in themselves and each other. I love how Miryem, Wanda and Irina were expected to be pallid and weak, pitiful things incapable of avenging themselves or anyone and only managing to pick up the tatters and mend them into wearable lives, but their unending anger at a world who refused to be exactly, enduringly the way they wanted it to be prompted them be <em>so much more</em>.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Let him think he had me, and could have my heart for the lifting of his finger. Let him think I would betray my people and my home just to be a queen beside him. He could hold my hand the rest of the way if he wanted to, as a fair return for the gift he’d given me, the one thing I’d wanted from him after all: I’d lost even the slightest qualm about killing him.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />I also love how we settle very early into a thwarted hatred for the "villains"—the tsar and the Staryk king—only for it to be reshaped and sculpted into the closest thing to empathy and affection there is.<br /><br />I just love how our perception of the characters ebb and flow over the course of the story, as the book provocatively illustrates the multidimensionality of someone considered to be a monster. Everything simple and solid in the characters' lives is made fluid and nuanced by the introduction of their true motives and feelings. And I think anyone would have found it difficult to be clued in to all the secret halls and trapdoors their souls held, and what each one hid and guarded, and not however grudgingly be moved by it. Because this is their story, too, all that had been hidden under flames and rivers of gold. And we’ve seen their journeys begin and end and begin again and we witnessed both the birth and culmination of their adventure, and so, by the time we close the book, the boundaries that barred their way have become thresholds made to be crossed, and we’ve walked with all these characters across each one, glancing back, but always moving forward.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“There are men who are wolves inside, and want to eat up other people to fill their bellies. That is what was in your house with you, all your life. But here you are with your brothers, and you are not eaten up, and there is not a wolf inside you. You have fed each other, and you kept the wolf away. <strong>That is all we can do for each other in the world, to keep the wolf away.” </strong></em>
</blockquote><br /><br />This is genuinely one of the best and most engrossing books I've read this year and one you definitely do not want to miss!<br /><br /><blockquote>✨ <a href="http://amzn.eu/9Jnbkf3" rel="nofollow noopener">wishlist</a> ✨ <a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ✨ <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ✨ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ✨</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="484410138722789255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2241121688" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2241121688" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2241121688?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399180989" href="/book/show/37168303-spinning-silver">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2241121688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4454370818406790397"><blockquote>
  <i>Because that's what the story is really about: getting out of paying your debts.</i>
</blockquote><br/>There is just something about Novik's fairy tales. Something <b>magical, atmospheric and utterly charming</b>. I didn't like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36896898.Spinning_Silver' title='Spinning Silver by Naomi Novik' rel='nofollow noopener'>Spinning Silver</a> quite as much as my beloved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted' title='Uprooted by Naomi Novik' rel='nofollow noopener'>Uprooted</a> - and I'll explain why a bit later - but it still kept me captivated from start to finish.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36896898.Spinning_Silver' title='Spinning Silver by Naomi Novik' rel='nofollow noopener'>Spinning Silver</a> is a loose retelling of <i>Rumpelstiltskin</i>. I say "loose" because you will recognise certain elements from the original - turning things into </span>
  <span id="freeText4454370818406790397" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Because that's what the story is really about: getting out of paying your debts.</i>
</blockquote><br />There is just something about Novik's fairy tales. Something <b>magical, atmospheric and utterly charming</b>. I didn't like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36896898.Spinning_Silver" title="Spinning Silver by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Spinning Silver</a> quite as much as my beloved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a> - and I'll explain why a bit later - but it still kept me captivated from start to finish.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36896898.Spinning_Silver" title="Spinning Silver by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Spinning Silver</a> is a loose retelling of <i>Rumpelstiltskin</i>. I say "loose" because you will recognise certain elements from the original - turning things into gold, the importance of names, etc. - but this is really a completely different story with different characters and many new plot lines. There's also not just one Rumpelstiltskin character, as several characters embody different aspects of the traditional imp.<br /><br />I love that it's a very pastoral fairy tale with forests and country magic. The setting of the book gives it a lot of its atmosphere, and it works very well. There are parts that follow the characters through quiet daily farming activities, but there is <b>magic and fear thrumming just under the surface</b>.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Blue shadows stretched out over the snow, cast by a pale thin light shining somewhere behind me, and as my breath rose in quick clouds around my face, the snow crunched: some large creature, picking its way toward the sleigh.</i>
</blockquote><br />Miryem is the daughter of the town's moneylender, but she takes over her father's job when he repeatedly fails to collect their debts. Turns out she has a talent for it and she soon finds herself turning more and more silver into gold. Unfortunately, this attracts the attention of one of the Staryk - fearsome creatures who desire gold above all else.<br /><br />I found it really interesting that Novik explored the idea of a Jewish moneylender as Rumpelstiltskin. The traditional story is one where Rumpelstiltskin aids a woman in spinning straw into gold and she refuses to hold up her side of the bargain. Interestingly, it is Rumpelstiltskin who is viewed as the greedy villain. Antisemitic interpretations of the story shed a completely new light on it. Though it was unlikely the intention of the original, as the folktale predates any record of antisemitismm by about 2000 years and predates the idea of the Jewish moneylender by even more, many believe that more modern Rumpelstiltskins were deliberately made to represent Jews.<br /><br />Novik, who is herself of Lithuanian-Jewish descent, uses this to challenge the Jewish moneylender stereotype and explore the antisemitism surrounding it. It's clever, and I loved it.<br /><br />In some ways, it is a smarter book than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a>, and yet I didn't like it quite as much because parts of this were definitely convoluted. What I've explained above is just a tiny portion of the plot. There are other supporting subplots involving a noblewoman marrying a tsar possessed by a fire demon, and a poor farm girl and her brother running away from a crime. Then there's the whole tale of the ice king and answering three questions every night. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Thrice, mortal maiden,” in a rhyme almost like a song, “Thrice you shall turn silver to gold for me, or be changed to ice yourself.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I counted no less than <b>six different perspectives</b> - honestly, I may have missed someone - and you have to learn the symbol/image for each character, as that is the only way you'll know whose point-of-view the book has moved to.<br /><br />Though I appreciate books with multiple layers and complex plots, I think shedding some parts of this would have only benefited it. Some chapters lean away from complex and interesting, and toward dense and confusing.<br /><br />That being said, I still recommend it if you enjoyed Novik's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a>. It's a fascinating, exciting fairy tale with a whole lot of atmosphere and charm. And creepy secret worlds on the other side of mirrors(!). I hope Novik writes more of these books soon.<br /><br />CW: Domestic abuse (physical; non-sexual); antisemitism. <br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4454370818406790397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2602699972" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2602699972" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2602699972?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=books-i-would-blurb">books-i-would-blurb</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2602699972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12185685328988173817">One of the best books I've read all year. Maybe THE best.<br/><br/>Good language. Excellent take on traditional faerie tale tropes. Brilliant storytelling. Amazing characterization.<br/><br/>There's nothing not to like here, honestly. And I'm going to be buying several copies as Christmas gifts for sure.</span>

          </span>

      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2602699972">

<div id="review_2222346696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2222346696" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2222346696?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399180989" href="/book/show/37168303-spinning-silver">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2222346696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6536229417502069284"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1530135433i/25869576._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC provided by Dey Rey in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Bring me the winter king, and I will make you a summer queen.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Spinning Silver</i> is one of the best books I’ve read all year. I loved this story with every fiber of my being. And Naomi Novik is a master at storytelling and interweaving stories together. You all know that this is a very loose reimaging of <i>Rumpelstiltskin</i> but I’d say it’s more of an empowering tale of three girls, all on three different paths, all promised to three</span>
  <span id="freeText6536229417502069284" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1530135433i/25869576._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC provided by Dey Rey in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Bring me the winter king, and I will make you a summer queen.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>Spinning Silver</i> is one of the best books I’ve read all year. I loved this story with every fiber of my being. And Naomi Novik is a master at storytelling and interweaving stories together. You all know that this is a very loose reimaging of <i>Rumpelstiltskin</i> but I’d say it’s more of an empowering tale of three girls, all on three different paths, all promised to three different men, while all being looked over by three different mothers. Three is such a constant theme in this book, too, and it really helps reinforce that this story feels like a tangible piece of magic in your hands while reading. This book is nothing short of a masterpiece. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The real story isn’t half as pretty as the one you’ve heard.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>The Three Girls: </u>
</b><br>➽ <b>Wanda</b> - a girl who has had to be strong, because it’s the only life she has ever known. Wanda has spent her short life taking care of her brothers and trying to please a father who is impossible to please. But that all changes once she is the only way to pay back his debts. <br>➽ <b>Irinushka</b> - a girl who has been born into royalty but has never known love from her blood family. Irina is still determined to save her people, by any means necessary. <br>➽ <b>Miryem</b> - a girl who will do whatever it takes to save her family. Miryem is strong, and relentless, and one of the very best characters I’ve ever read in my entire life. And she becomes one of the most feared moneylenders in her village, and she discovers that she awfully good at turning silver to gold. But she is not the only one that notices. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“That part of the old story turned out to be true: you have to be cruel to be a good moneylender. But I was ready to be as merciless.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>The Three Mothers: </u>
</b><br>➽ <b>A Passed Away Mother</b> who continues to look after her children.<br>➽ <b>An Adoptive Mother</b> who has unconditionally loved her child from the start. <br>➽ <b>A Birth Mother</b> who wants nothing more than her child safe and happy.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“A robber who steals a knife and cuts himself cannot cry out against the woman who kept it sharp.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>The Three Marriages: </u>
</b><br>➽ <b>Filled with Hate</b> because even in 2018 some men want to believe that they know what’s best for a woman, no matter the cost. <br>➽ <b>Filled with Fire</b> because some people are born into a world without a chance, regardless of money, power, and privilege.<br>➽ <b>Filled with Cold</b> because protecting the thing you love is sometimes something you’re willing to do anything for. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“...someone had climbed down and looked through our window: someone wearing strange boots with a long pointed toe.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And these three girls, with their mothers, forced into their three marriages, all come together and create something so beautiful that I don’t even have words to express it. I will say that Miryem is for sure the main character. I will also say that we get to see a lot more points of view than these three girls and their betrothals. And the story is something that is so whimsical, so feminist, and nothing short of an honor to read. <br><br><b>Trigger and content warnings</b> for hard scenes to read about loss of a parent, siblings, and death of children, for extreme parental physical abuse, brief mention of animal deaths, mention of past rape, sexual assault, alcoholism, torture, violence, murder, and use of the word Jew (not negatively, but it still didn’t feel good to read at times). <br><br>But one thing I did want to touch upon is how much Judaism plays such an integral role in this story. Miryem and her entire family are Jewish, and from the first to last page this plays a pivotal role in the story. I am not Jewish, but I still loved this inclusion so very much. Also, I’m adding “go to a Jewish wedding” onto my bucket list immediately. To my Jewish friends: please, invite me to your weddings. <br><br><i>Spinning Silver</i> is such a love letter to found families everywhere, too. You guys know I love reading about found families, but all three girls in this book are the epitome of found families. Unconditional love is truly the strongest force in this universe, and not only does this book showcase that, it also celebrates that. <br><br>Overall, this just felt like a story that was single-handedly created for me. From the Staryks, to the Winter King, to the traveling between places, to the so very strong female cast, to the magic, to every single word on every single page. I swear, opening this book felt like magic and I never wanted to shut it. And I know I am being rather vague with my synopsis, but I truly believe that this book is probably best to go in not knowing much, and to just experience this otherworldly story firsthand. Without a doubt, this will make my “best of 2018” list and will forever have a place on my favorites of all-time shelf. Thank you so much, Naomi Novik, for a story I will cherish forever. And that last line will take my breath away every reread. Perfection. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Because that’s what the story’s really about: getting out of paying your debts.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><i>The quotes above were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6536229417502069284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2441199679" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2441199679" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2441199679?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781509899012" href="/book/show/38606192-spinning-silver">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2441199679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10828628686347638541"><b>This novel is pure escapism; it is enchanting, mystical and, most importantly, it's a fantastic piece of writing. <u>I loved it.</u> Go read it!</b><br/><br/>I’m a critic but I found nothing to critique here. And for me that says a lot. I often find it hard just to sit back and enjoy a story without pulling it apart and dissecting all the elements of the book. It’s just want happens when you’re and English student. You consider the characters, the themes and everything the writing is trying to convey. With this, how</span>
  <span id="freeText10828628686347638541" style="display:none"><b>This novel is pure escapism; it is enchanting, mystical and, most importantly, it's a fantastic piece of writing. <u>I loved it.</u> Go read it!</b><br /><br />I’m a critic but I found nothing to critique here. And for me that says a lot. I often find it hard just to sit back and enjoy a story without pulling it apart and dissecting all the elements of the book. It’s just want happens when you’re and English student. You consider the characters, the themes and everything the writing is trying to convey. With this, however, I was taken away by the majestic nature of the fairy-tale plot. It all just fitted together so perfectly and slid into an ending that left me feeling warm inside. <br /><br />The novel is an amalgamation of fairy tales, all distinctively eastern European in feel, though they are fleshed out and twisted into something resembling a complex and compelling story that is not limited by the standard tropes fairy tales demand. This is not a novel about love; it is one about survival in a cut-throat world where the rich and powerful exploit the poor, weak and helpless. The peasants starve in the winter as their lands are raided by the mystical Staryk whilst their Tsar hordes the entire kingdom’s wealth and basks in his own splendour. He does little to help his own people.<br /><br />As such, people have to learn to survive and defend themselves in an unjust world. There are no heroes, only people who are willing to be brave in the face of tyranny. And tyranny can come in many forms, and often those who are supposed to love and protect us become the worse of the lot. Daughters learn to overthrow their fathers and make their own paths in the world. Miryem learns to turn silver into gold by taking up her father’s money lending business, and eventually what appears to be a natural aptitude for business develops into a fully-fledged magical ability that captures the attention of an Ice King. <br /><br />From here the plot only improves. There are a multitude of characters and point of views though they are all linked and brought together into such a powerful ending. As Miryem is taken back to the Staryk kingdom, the Tsar daemon of rage and fire seeks to melt the lands of always winter. Two conflicting powers come crashing together, as the veil is lifted revealing the truth of a character shrouded in misunderstanding and ice. Just because a people operate in a different way, it does not make them inherently evil.<br /><br /><i>Spinning Silver</i> is so much better than <i>Uprooted</i> because it is consistent; it sticks with the same themes and develops them until the very end of the story rather than shifting into a radical new plot line half-way through the story. As such the magic begins on the very first page and stays until the very last- <b>
  <u>I highly recommend it! </u>
</b><br /><br />___________________________________<br /><br />You can connect with me on social media via <a href="https://linktr.ee/sean.ultra_vegan1" rel="nofollow noopener">My Linktree</a>.<br />__________________________________</span>

<div id="review_2263529406" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2263529406" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2263529406?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781509899012" href="/book/show/38606192-spinning-silver">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=east-europe-russia">east-europe-russia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=faerie">faerie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2263529406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3057624966220649148">All the stars!! One of my favorite fantasies ever ... I think it's officially part of my desert island collection. Review first posted on <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/spinning-silver/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>: <br/><br/>It’s not often that I end a novel in awe of characters, the world-building, and the depth and complexity of the themes, while still being absolutely delighted with the storytelling. In <i>Spinning Silver</i>, Naomi Novik does all that and more.<br/><br/>In medieval Lithvas (according to Novik, a fantasy version of Lithuania with a little Russia and Poland b</span>
  <span id="freeText3057624966220649148" style="display:none">All the stars!! One of my favorite fantasies ever ... I think it's officially part of my desert island collection. Review first posted on <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/spinning-silver/" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>: <br><br>It’s not often that I end a novel in awe of characters, the world-building, and the depth and complexity of the themes, while still being absolutely delighted with the storytelling. In <i>Spinning Silver</i>, Naomi Novik does all that and more.<br><br>In medieval Lithvas (according to Novik, a fantasy version of Lithuania with a little Russia and Poland blended in), Miryem Mandelstam is the daughter of a Jewish moneylender in a small town. Panov Mandelstam is a gentle, kindhearted man: too kind to be a successful moneylender, in fact, since he’s constitutionally unable to demand repayment of the money he’s lent out, leaving him and his wife and daughter destitute. When her mother falls ill, Miryam has had enough. A bit of winter has found its way into her heart, and that combined with her stubbornness (and her threats to involve her wealthy grandfather and the law if the villagers don’t repay her what they owe) makes her a success at her new job as village moneylender.<br><br>Miryem takes on a strong village girl, Wanda, as a household servant, letting her work off her father’s debt. Miryam doesn’t realize it, but Wanda is actually grateful for the chance to avoid her abusive father, and to stealthily put away the extra money that Miryam pays her. Miryam’s parents are alarmed at the increased iciness in her heart, but she has no intention of handing the moneylending job back to her ineffective father. Miryam rather defiantly tells her mother that she shouldn’t be sorry that her daughter has the ability to change silver into gold.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534199631i/26123814.jpg" width="300" height="227" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However, there’s a magical road that appears and disappears in Lithvas during the winter, controlled by the fae-like Staryk, and other ears have heard Miryam’s boast to her mother during her journey back to their village. Soon she finds herself entangled in the Staryk king’s demands to change his silver into gold. Miryam comes up with a brilliant plan, but meeting the Staryk king’s demands may be almost as bad as failure.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534198572i/26123778.png" width="282" height="356" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(I get a Thranduil vibe from the Staryk king, except ... needs more ice)<br><br><i>Spinning Silver</i> begins with these allusions to the Rumpelstiltskin fairy tale, but Novik is weaving far more into her story than this one tale. Miryam’s plan involves the ambitious duke of Vysnia and his daughter Irina, who is thought too plain to attract the handsome young tsar of Lithvas, Mirnatius. The Staryk silver may tip the balance for Irina, but she soon finds that gaining Mirnatius’s attention is a highly dangerous thing indeed. Irina’s story quickly becomes as compelling as Miryam’s, as she needs to use all her wits and some gifts of her heritage to escape with her life and soul intact.<br><br>Novik’s unique moneylender twist on the story of Rumpelstiltskin is highly creative. Eastern European folklore is woven in as well. The (literally) icy Staryk king and his winter kingdom called to mind Morozko, the Russian frost-king, and I had an appreciative shudder of recognition when a certain fiery demon is named. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534199258i/26123801.png" width="321" height="285" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(hat tip to Marvel for the Surtur image)<br><br>Novik takes her story far beyond a retelling or recasting of old tales, though. I particularly enjoyed the fascinating concepts dealing with cold Staryk silver and the warm gold from the “sunlit world.” It played into the plot in a way that I hadn’t anticipated.<br><br>The sensitive, meaningful way in which the Jewish faith and culture were incorporated into <i>Spinning Silver</i> was lovely. Antisemitism is addressed, but doesn’t weigh down the story. The focus is more on personal connections, like the love between Irina and her old nurse, the understanding and respect that Miryam gains for the Staryk people, and the family bonds that develop between the Mandelstams and Wanda and her brothers.<br><br>Without tipping over into unrealistic anachronism, we also see women characters who are empowered by the actions they take to save themselves, as well as others they care about, in spite of the fact that each of them ― against their desires ― is promised, given, or simply taken in marriage. It’s a fairly subtle connection between our three main characters.<br><br><i>Spinning Silver</i> is an enchanting fantasy, woven of fire and ice, sunlit gold and Staryk silver, icy faerie winter and Lithvas spring. Naomi Novik has crafted a truly wondrous novel.<br><br><b>Initial posts:</b> The author of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a> strikes again, with what appears to be a take-off on Rumpelstiltskin. Can't wait for July!!<br><br>ETA: I'm dying here. I didn't get the ARC (the publicist was unmoved by my sad email) and my local library, which I thought would jump right on this one, still doesn't have it in their catalog. I HAVE BROKEN DOWN AND BOUGHT THE DANG BOOK. In hardback, no less. Stay posted!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3057624966220649148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2263538056" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2263538056" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2263538056?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fairytale">fairytale</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2263538056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6074659527385830032">Ok. This is a retelling of Rumplestiltskin...but not. <br/>What I mean is, Novik <i>really</i> took the idea of spinning straw to gold and the importance of a name, and just made that shit her own new story.<br/><i>*tips hat*</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543165153ra/26647141.gif' width='400' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So, in this fairytale Eastern European<i>ish</i> setting, there's this spunky little Jewish girl named Miryem that kicks ass and takes names. She ends up with not only all the normal problems an ambitious female minority would have, but also the extra (and quite HUGE) problem of doing impossible thing</span>
  <span id="freeText6074659527385830032" style="display:none">Ok. This is a retelling of Rumplestiltskin...but not. <br>What I mean is, Novik <i>really</i> took the idea of spinning straw to gold and the importance of a name, and just made that shit her own new story.<br><i>*tips hat*</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543165153ra/26647141.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, in this fairytale Eastern European<i>ish</i> setting, there's this spunky little Jewish girl named Miryem that kicks ass and takes names. She ends up with not only all the normal problems an ambitious female minority would have, but also the extra (and quite HUGE) problem of doing impossible things to keep the assy king of the (scary as hell) winter fairies (called Staryk) that live in the woods from doing scary as hell stuff to her. &lt;--kinda?<br><b>But Miryem is not one to be cowed by some bitchy fairy king.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542897860ra/26634251.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then you've got Irina. A dumpy duke's daughter whose father uses some shady means (and a pinch of Staryk silver) to get the (creepy as fuck) tsar to marry her. She soon finds out that her not so beloved has a <i>teeny</i> little secret that just might get her eaten alive by more than just his court of petty nobles. Apparently, making a deal with a demon can backfire on you. &lt;--who knew?<br><b>But Irina is tougher than she looks.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542899730ra/26634383.gif" width="350" height="275" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then there's Wanda. This poor kid is just trying to survive her abusive home life when she gets pulled into the story by Miryem. Who, by the way, is only using her to collect a debt from her father. &lt;--in case you were under the impression that our girl was a sweetheart.<br>And maybe at first Wanda is just hanging on for dear life, but somewhere along the way she finds her voice.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542902359ra/26634532.gif" width="400" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then there's the rest of this <i>enormous</i> cast of characters...<br>The POV changes in this thing are unreal. I lost track of how many voices there eventually were, to be honest. The pacing wasn't exactly breakneck, but in my opinion, the story was worth plodding through some of the more meandering parts. But if you're not a fan of books that you have to chew and chew and chew? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542902359ra/26634533.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Well, you've been warned.</b><br>This was a <b>thick-ass</b> book and the length took me by surprise in the way that only an e-book can. You know what I mean? When you go in and grab a physical copy of something, and then your arm comes out of socket when you try to lift it up...you know what you're getting yourself into. But when you download a book? There's that moment when you realize that you've been reading for an hour and you're only 4% done with the thing. Always fun...<br>Normally, I'm not a fan of stuff that doesn't hop along at a good clip, but Novak just turns my crank when it comes to storytelling, so she can get away with these wonky-ass long stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6074659527385830032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2302296495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2302296495" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2302296495?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399180989" href="/book/show/37168303-spinning-silver">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=faery-tales">faery-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=best-of-2018">best-of-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2302296495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13124765668847669768"><i>“I am not your subject or your servant, and if you want a cowering mouse for a wife, go find someone else who can turn silver to gold for you.”</i> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533021958ra/26054235.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was a buddy read with my elvish friend, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2451797478?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Maica</a>! I’m so glad that we decided to read this together! <3<br/><br/><b>Confession Time:</b> I was a bit scared going into this because I loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted' title='Uprooted by Naomi Novik' rel='nofollow noopener'>Uprooted</a> so bloody much. And how on Earth could Naomi Novik possibly improve upon that <i>pure and utter perfection</i>, which included wizards, royals, tree people, and all sorts of other f</span>
  <span id="freeText13124765668847669768" style="display:none"><i>“I am not your subject or your servant, and if you want a cowering mouse for a wife, go find someone else who can turn silver to gold for you.”</i> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533021958ra/26054235.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was a buddy read with my elvish friend, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2451797478?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Maica</a>! I’m so glad that we decided to read this together! &lt;3<br><br><b>Confession Time:</b> I was a bit scared going into this because I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a> so bloody much. And how on Earth could Naomi Novik possibly improve upon that <i>pure and utter perfection</i>, which included wizards, royals, tree people, and all sorts of other fun characters? Well, somehow, unbeknownst to me, Novik managed to do just that! Now <b>this</b> is a faery tale retelling. Naomi Novik might have just shoved Rosamund Hodge to the side as my favourite author, in regards to retellings!!!<br><br>Now before I get into this novel, as someone who was raised as inter-faith (half-Anglican, half-Jewish), I absolutely <i>adored</i> the <b>Jewish representation</b> in this novel!!! Do you know how rare it is, aside from World War Two or Holocaust novels? With the exception of Simon Lewis from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/44457-the-mortal-instruments" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mortal Instruments</a>, I can’t even remember the last time that I came across a Jewish minor-character in a series, much less having it be a fundamental part of the story!!! From Shabbat to weddings to prayers, I loved the inclusion of Jewish culture!<br><br>However, having said that, I would like to point out that there is quite a bit of <b>antisemitism</b> in this novel, as well…So, fair warning, if that’s something that you don’t want to read about.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36896898.Spinning_Silver" title="Spinning Silver by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Spinning Silver</a> is an exquisite and <i>atmospheric, pastoral wintery tale</i> told from the perspectives of not one, not two, but <b>three female protagonists</b>, in addition to a few others along the way. But not to worry, each perspective has a very distinctive voice, and I found it very easy to differentiate between them. I also found that the <b>slow pacing</b> of this novel definitely added to its charm, as you begin to anticipate the various storylines finally coming together. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533022205ra/26054251.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Miryem</b> is a young Jewish woman whose father is a rather poor moneylender. He is far too generous, by not demanding borrowers to repay their debts, which is not conducive to putting food on the table. Thus, she takes up his occupation in order to save her family from cold and starvation. She is very smart and shrewd, and is more than happy to strike a good bargain!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533021958ra/26054237.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Wanda</b> is a beautiful girl who comes from an abusive family because her father is a gambling drunkard, who does not contribute to the household at all. He treats his children more like hired help than young adolescents. She eventually finds a positon in Miryem’s household, in order to pay off her father’s debts. She also has two younger brothers, Sergey and Stepon, to feed and support, as well. She is a very strong and responsible older sister.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533022205ra/26054252.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Irina</b> is the unattractive daughter of a Duke. Since her mother was a descendant of the Staryk (elf/fae-type creature) and because her dowry was magical, Staryk silver, she was able to be married off to the reluctant tsar, Mirnatius. She was very caring towards others and thought quite carefully when making very difficult decisions. She is a rather wonderful tsarina, who inspired loyalty in others.<br><br>As was the case with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a> (a loose Beauty and the Beast retelling), this is not a strict <b>Rumpelstiltskin retelling</b> either. In fact, I found references to various other faery tales and mythologies, which was very exciting, considering that my knowledge of <i>Slavic folklore</i> is virtually non-existent. It takes place in a setting comparable to Lithuania, with an unexplained magic system, as is the case with most faery tales. Explaining everything would ruin the spell that this novel shall cast on you! ;)<br><br>However, if I were being honest, my absolute favourite part of this novel was the <b>family dynamics</b>. There was <i>so much emphasis</i> put on a familial bond. It was so lovely to read about because oftentimes, I’ve found that as stories progress, family members tend to mysteriously disappear or are never actually involved. Neither of which occurs here. <br><br>I absolutely loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36896898.Spinning_Silver" title="Spinning Silver by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Spinning Silver</a> and I would definitely recommend this to anyone who enjoys faery tale retellings, especially ones such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25489134.The_Bear_and_the_Nightingale__Winternight_Trilogy___1_" title="The Bear and the Nightingale (Winternight Trilogy, #1) by Katherine Arden" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bear and the Nightingale</a>. Naomi Novik is such an <i>imaginative writer</i>, with such a <i>whimsical writing style</i> that I would hate for you to miss it! …Although for the life of me, I can’t understand why it was released in July! :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="13124765668847669768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2461601681" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2461601681" />
    <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale"><img alt="Hannah Greendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466436186p2/43377498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2461601681?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781509899012" href="/book/show/38606192-spinning-silver">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=mythology-folklore">mythology-folklore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2461601681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12289571146934997880">Novik introduces three daring female protagonists in this clever re-imagining of Rumpelstiltskin. Here is a realm of magic and mysticism, of cruelty and heartbreak, fringed with glittering ice and populated with creatures carved from the wildest corners of the imagination. The initial chapters titillate with high stakes, compelling characters, and enchanting descriptions of warm food and a forest cloaked in snow, but the narrative is soon bogged down by several ruinous flaws. <br/><br/>Despite encounterin</span>
  <span id="freeText12289571146934997880" style="display:none">Novik introduces three daring female protagonists in this clever re-imagining of Rumpelstiltskin. Here is a realm of magic and mysticism, of cruelty and heartbreak, fringed with glittering ice and populated with creatures carved from the wildest corners of the imagination. The initial chapters titillate with high stakes, compelling characters, and enchanting descriptions of warm food and a forest cloaked in snow, but the narrative is soon bogged down by several ruinous flaws. <br /><br />Despite encountering wondrous and unexpected forms of magic, Novik's characters are neither astonished nor surprised. Their flat response evokes a perpetual sense of apathy, a problem that's exacerbated by glacial pacing, further compounded by two of the female protagonists having such similar plot lines as to feel redundant. <br /><br />The final nail in the coffin - or icicle in the heart - is the inclusion of multiple POVs. Novik opens with two primary voices, but more characters are introduced as the story progresses. A change in POV is indicated by an icon of a spinning wheel, but the speaker is not identified and new character voices are dropped without preamble. Not only does this create extra work and confusion, Novik elects to recount scenes from varied perspectives, resulting in even more redundancy.<br /><br /><i>Spinning Silver</i> holds all the ingredients of a magic spell, but the execution leaves one cold and unsatisfied.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12289571146934997880" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2654006107" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2654006107" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2654006107?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=axis360">axis360</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2654006107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17563924153505084860">Spinning Silver by Naomi Novik is a 2018 Del Rey publication. <br/><br/>I need more stories like this one in my life! <br/><br/> I rarely grab a fantasy novel, although, I am often tempted by them. I respect the genre immensely because of the thoughtfulness and work required for world building and the huge imaginations of fantasy writers. However, no matter how badly I might want to dive into a high fantasy, I always manage to talk myself out of it. My first excuse usually has to with the heft of the book, and the </span>
  <span id="freeText17563924153505084860" style="display:none">Spinning Silver by Naomi Novik is a 2018 Del Rey publication. <br /><br />I need more stories like this one in my life! <br /><br /> I rarely grab a fantasy novel, although, I am often tempted by them. I respect the genre immensely because of the thoughtfulness and work required for world building and the huge imaginations of fantasy writers. However, no matter how badly I might want to dive into a high fantasy, I always manage to talk myself out of it. My first excuse usually has to with the heft of the book, and the sheer concentration required on my part, as fantasy usually requires a bit more of my undivided attention. With so many books I need to read, taking time out for an epic fantasy feels like a daunting endeavor. <br /><br />However, this book kept popping up on my Goodreads feed, and it happens to be a stand- alone, not a part of an ongoing epic saga, <b>AND</b> it is marketed as a re-telling of the classic Grimm fairy-tale, <i>Rumpelstiltskin</i>, which was one of my favorite stories as a child, a story own children enjoyed too, plus it comes in at just under five hundred pages, which is doable. <br />The bare bones set up is something like this: <br /><br /> Miryem Mandelstam’s father is a Jewish money-lender, but he’s not very good at his job. He lends money easily enough, but usually fails to collect when the payments are due, which has put his family in serious financial straits. So, Miryem takes over for her father, with far better results. She then hires, Wanda, whose abusive father owes her money, to work off his debt by being her assistant. <br /><br />Miryem’s success attracts the attention of the ‘Staryk’, fairies, who thrive only in the frigid cold winter. From here, Miryem gets caught in a vicious cycle, as The Winter King forces her to continue turning silver into gold. <br /><br />Meanwhile, Irina, a plain lady in waiting, from the same city as Miryem’s wealthy maternal grandparents, becomes attractive to everyone around her, with the help of a magical Fae crown. This development helps her father convince the Tsar to marry her. However, the Tsar is rumored to have delved into the black arts and his soul is demon possessed. <br /><br />First, let me address the <i>Rumpelstiltskin</i> parallels. Yes, there are obvious references to the class fable, however, in my humble opinion, the book goes far beyond a re-telling. In fact, the story seems to also borrow from several other folk legends, as well. <br /><br />There is a lot going on with the three featured women in the story, all of whom face different challenges and meet those challenges with bravery and cunning. While the fairy-tale has gotten a lot of bad press in recent years, I have never wavered from believing they served a greater purpose. Okay- sure there is a usually a happy ending, (God forbid!) but, there is more dark reality in these tales of folklore than meets the eye, and they nearly always come with a built- in lesson of morality. This story also comes replete with tons of allegory and symbolism, the most notable being that of antisemitism. <br /><br />The story is absolutely mesmerizing, so rich in detail, and imagery, with layers upon layers of thought -provoking situations, in which our characters face evil, greed, and life or death situations.<br /><br /> The one downfall is that the book is often poorly structured, with breakneck shifts in narratives, which took me out of the story, forcing me to slow down and re-read segments to be sure I was staying up with who was doing or saying what. I really dislike this type of issue in any book I read, but it is especially annoying when it occurs in a genre where large casts of characters are prevalent and so much important dialogue and activity is in play. The momentum, which is not really designed to move at a brisk pace, still suffered, as a result of this rather unorthodox setup. Once I knew what to expect, however, I was prepared for the sudden shifts and eventually adjusted to the jarring style. <br /><br />Other than that, reading this book was an incredible experience. I loved the way the story paid homage to the types of fairytales I loved, putting a fresh spin on favorite tropes, featuring three strong female leads, and still managed to incorporate faith and religion into the tale, in a new and refreshing way, giving the reader something substantial to digest. <br /><br />This is my first book by this author, and I feel I may be showing up a little late to the party. But, after losing myself in this gem of a story, I’m inspired to read more of Novik's work. Not only that, immersing myself in this story helped to stave off a rapidly building burnout phase. <br /><br />It’s time to slow down the conveyor belt on ARC’s and the pressure of deadlines and blog posts, and social media and all the rest, and escape into an epic fantasy tome more often. I need to enjoy more books I’ve been missing out on, more classics, more vintage books, and more reading simply for the pleasure of reading. <br /><br /> Here’s to more world building, to more fantasy and epic sagas, and to taking a long overdue vacation!!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17563924153505084860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2444548659?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" href="/user/show/16219087-chelsea-chelseadolling-reads">Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2444548659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11570579552634137924">No one freak out, but I just thoroughly enjoyed a fantasy book 😍 this was so immersive and well written and I liked it a heckin’ ton! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2644215053" class="readable"
