<span id="freeTextContainer12518071636662577732"><b>Novik has the golden touch—there is richness of writing, richness of setting and richness of characterisation.</b><br/><br/><i>Spinning Silver</i> was vividly evocative—an artful rendering of snow swirling ghostlike against slate-smeared skies, of crimson flames licking hungrily at the winter air. And there was something about it that was so irresistibly beguiling, thawing my cynical adult heart. <br/>I admired Miryem, Wanda and Irina—all of whom, despite the burden of their circumstance, rose up and raised their heads h</span>
  <span id="freeText12518071636662577732" style="display:none"><b>Novik has the golden touch—there is richness of writing, richness of setting and richness of characterisation.</b><br><br><i>Spinning Silver</i> was vividly evocative—an artful rendering of snow swirling ghostlike against slate-smeared skies, of crimson flames licking hungrily at the winter air. And there was something about it that was so irresistibly beguiling, thawing my cynical adult heart. <br>I admired Miryem, Wanda and Irina—all of whom, despite the burden of their circumstance, rose up and raised their heads high, undaunted and unafraid. I admired their strength and determination, the fierceness of their resolve to protect the people important to them. And in the end, each of them created more from the little that'd been afforded to them, weaving the threads of their life into something that was rich, beautiful and full of meaning.<br><br><i>Spinning Silver</i> would be perfect, if not for <b>the choppy pacing and paragraphs <i>upon</i> paragraphs of utterly useless scene-setting. </b>While I am <i>all</i> for descriptive writing, I'd prefer to do without the overly mundane detail, please.<br>And asides from doing nothing, the descriptions <i>did</i> sap the plot of its momentum and me of my patience. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1592908128ra/29693889.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And yet, be that as it may, I did love <i>Spinning Silver</i>—I loved it <b>for its compelling, rich characters and quaint, picturesque settings, for its limpid prose and enchanting, fairytale-like charm.</b><br><br>4.0/5</span>

<div id="review_2470035625" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2470035625" />
    <a title="Angelica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16201093-angelica"><img alt="Angelica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507050077p2/16201093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2470035625?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angelica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angelica" href="/user/show/16201093-angelica">Angelica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399180989" href="/book/show/37168303-spinning-silver">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=fairytales">fairytales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=cool-tittle">cool-tittle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=release-2018">release-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=five-star">five-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2470035625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer28177572949121189"><b>Ok, so I’m officially impressed?</b><br/><br/>I was feeling a bit wary about picking this book up when I first heard about it. I head read Naomi Novik’s other book, Uprooted, a book that had was nominated for both the Nebula and Hugo awards for best fantasy, and even won the Nebula. And you know what? I hated it.<br/><br/>So, as you can imagine, I wasn’t too sure about this one. Then on a whim, I got it as my Book of the Month, and I decided to read it. Now, all I have to say is that Naomi Novik has found herself a new</span>
  <span id="freeText28177572949121189" style="display:none"><b>Ok, so I’m officially impressed?</b><br /><br />I was feeling a bit wary about picking this book up when I first heard about it. I head read Naomi Novik’s other book, Uprooted, a book that had was nominated for both the Nebula and Hugo awards for best fantasy, and even won the Nebula. And you know what? I hated it.<br /><br />So, as you can imagine, I wasn’t too sure about this one. Then on a whim, I got it as my Book of the Month, and I decided to read it. Now, all I have to say is that Naomi Novik has found herself a new fan in me.<br /><br /><b>This book is magical.</b> Truly, incredibly magical. From the world to characters, to the writing itself. Once I got into the story I couldn’t put it down. I actually read up until like three in the morning to read it.<br /><br />I’m not going to say much about the story because I want to spoil anything. But, know that the story follows three young women, Miryem, the daughter of a Jewish moneylender, Irinia, the daughter of a duke, and Wanda, the daughter of the town drunk. Of all of these, it is clear that Miryem’s story is at the center of this epic tale as it all begins and ends with her. Aside from these three, there are other small POV changes from supporting charcters that allow us to see the full scope of the tale.<br /><br />Throughout out the novel the three girls, all who had begun as seemingly weak and oppressed in some way or another, managed to shine and show the world just how much strength lay within them. I loved seeing them develop and grow into the power and opportunities they had each been given. I also love how they used their wit and determination to outsmart their oppressors and come out on top.<br /><br />My one complaint with this is that the POV changes were pretty random and were never announced. There would be a line break and suddenly, there would be a new person speaking from another part of the land and I would have no idea what was happening for a moment.<br /><br />Thankfully, it would only take me a paragraph or two before I realized whose POV I was in. If anything, I think that shows off Naomi Novik’s writing ability that I could so easily recognize which character was narrating the story. <b>There was the depth to each of the characters.</b> Even the ones who seemed most remote and cruel had so much passion in their souls. So much personality brimming through the pages.<br /><br /><b>And the writing!!!</b><br /><br />The writing was beautiful and atmospheric. Novik describes the winter in such beautiful ways, both as a thing of beauty and one of cruelty, sometimes as both. I wish I would have read this in the winter instead of the middle of summer because this would make the perfect winter read.<br /><br /><b>Other parts I loved about the story was the inclusion of Judaism as such a large part and Miryem’s life.</b> We rarely ever see a real religion in fantasy, and rarely are charcters so faithful to it without coming across as fanatic or portrayed in a negative light. And even more rarely is the religion mentioned Judaism. So, I highly appreciated how Miryem stayed true to her faith, even until the end.<br /><br />Overall, I highly recommend this book. If you like fantasy, or retellings, or good books in general, I would tell you to add this one to your TBR.<br /><br /><b>Seriously though, this book was amazing. Go read it!</b><br /><br /><br />Follow Me Here Too:<b> <a href="http://www.thebookcovergirls.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/covergirlreads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/book-cover-girl-19339391" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin'</a> || <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookcovergirls//" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://thebookcovergirls.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thebookcovergirls/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="28177572949121189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16650154177244477361">the only thing that has been spun is my never ending boredom. <br/><br/>while the silver strands were loosely woven in the beginning and partially spooled by a few enchantingly charming chapters, my attention eventually tangled and frayed away. <br/><br/>as with <i>uprooted</i>, this unraveling of enjoyment is most likely my fault and not the storys. because again, this is actually quite a beautiful fantasy concept and a remarkably unique retelling of a classic story. but i just couldnt get into it, the writing, the chara</span>
  <span id="freeText16650154177244477361" style="display:none">the only thing that has been spun is my never ending boredom. <br /><br />while the silver strands were loosely woven in the beginning and partially spooled by a few enchantingly charming chapters, my attention eventually tangled and frayed away. <br /><br />as with <i>uprooted</i>, this unraveling of enjoyment is most likely my fault and not the storys. because again, this is actually quite a beautiful fantasy concept and a remarkably unique retelling of a classic story. but i just couldnt get into it, the writing, the characters, the romances, or anything else.<br /><br />its been soooo long since i have found an author that i just dont click with and im really at a loss as to why. on paper, both <i>spinning silver</i> and <i>uprooted</i> should have been a wonderful reading experiences - they have everything i love in classic fantasy stories - but they both met the same unfortunate fate of my dying interest. <br /><br />sorry naomi novik - its not you, it me. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>2.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_2231335187" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2231335187" />
    <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc"><img alt="Mogsy (MMOGC)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286325553p2/4379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2231335187?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mogsy (MMOGC)" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc">Mogsy (MMOGC)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=arcs-and-galleys">arcs-and-galleys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=fairy-tales-and-folklore">fairy-tales-and-folklore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2231335187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10137001848073676143">3.5 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://bibliosanctum.com/2018/07/10/book-review-spinning-silver-by-naomi-novik/'>https://bibliosanctum.com/2018/07/10/...</a><br/><br/>I know I’m in the minority here, but I didn’t love this book. Oh, I enjoyed it well enough, because it’s Naomi Novik and her prose is always excellent, and Spinning Silver was beautifully written. However, I’ve also had enough experience with work (especially with the Temeraire series) to know her books can be very hit or miss. Believe me, I was thrilled when she started writing fairy-tale-inspired fantasy novels, and I </span>
  <span id="freeText10137001848073676143" style="display:none">3.5 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bibliosanctum.com/2018/07/10/book-review-spinning-silver-by-naomi-novik/">https://bibliosanctum.com/2018/07/10/...</a><br /><br />I know I’m in the minority here, but I didn’t love this book. Oh, I enjoyed it well enough, because it’s Naomi Novik and her prose is always excellent, and Spinning Silver was beautifully written. However, I’ve also had enough experience with work (especially with the Temeraire series) to know her books can be very hit or miss. Believe me, I was thrilled when she started writing fairy-tale-inspired fantasy novels, and I absolutely adored Uprooted, but I just wasn’t as taken with this one as I expected to be.<br /><br />The story of Spinning Silver contains several POVs, but the closest we have to a main protagonist is Miryem, the daughter of a very bad moneylender. Everyone knows her father will let late payments slide, and is too timid to chase down what is owed. As a result, Miryem’s family lives in poverty while her father’s borrowers flourish, until one day, our protagonist has had enough, and she sets out into the village to knock on the door of everyone with outstanding payments. And as it turns out, Miryem makes a rather formidable moneylender. Very quickly, she turns a pouch of silver pennies that her father loaned her into a big bag full of gold.<br /><br />But even more quickly, rumors of a girl who can change silver to gold began to spread far and wide, eventually reaching the ears of the Staryk, cold-hearted beings of folklore who desire gold and riches above anything else. Miryem catches the attention of their wintry ruler, who orders her to transform his vast stores of silver into gold, and in return he will make her his queen.<br /><br />First, I’ll go into what I loved about the book: the atmosphere and folksy fairy tale vibes that bring to mind the dark, mysterious charms of a Brothers Grimm story. If the plot of Spinning Silver reminded you a bit of Rumpelstiltskin, that’s because the novel is loosely inspired by that tale, though you’ll also likely catch snippets and elements from a lot of different fairy tales while reading. One of the most impressive things the author has done here is the way she incorporates these stories and their themes into a new narrative, focusing on relatable and genuine characters while still preserving a lot of the original wonder and magic. This has always been Naomi Novik’s forte whether she’s writing about dragons in the Napoleonic Wars or a persistent moneylender’s daughter from a rural village. Whenever she reimagines a world, she does it in a way that’s rooted in history and folkloric tradition, but the end result is always complex and creative enough to make it stand out from the rest.<br /><br />And now, for the things I didn’t like so much. Unfortunately for me, the second half of this book was kind of a slog. Part of the problem was Spinning Silver wasn’t just a story about Miryem, and over time, more characters are introduced to the mix. I didn’t mind it at first; Wanda for one was a wonderful new addition, and I loved the strength she showed even through hard, trying times. Then there was Irina, a girl born into the royal court, but while she may be rich in possessions, she is poor in love. Despite her upbringing though, she is selfless and caring, only wanting to do right by her people. Later on, however, we also have a few other minor POVs join their voices, and that’s where things started to get a little messy. First of all, I didn’t feel that all these perspectives were really necessary, as overall they didn’t add as much as I would have liked. Second, whereas I found myself completely rapt by the intro and first half of the novel, the rest of it felt convoluted and a bit bloated. Also, the book was probably longer than it had to be, which, admittedly, was an issue with Uprooted as well. The difference there was that I was able to push through some of the slower and more meandering parts, but here I found it was a struggle to even stay focused. It’s a shame because I loved the first half of the book, but the momentum and interest I found there did not extend all the way through to the end (though to be fair, things did pick up again just in time for the conclusion).<br /><br />Like I said, I enjoyed Spinning Silver, but I also don’t think it’s a standout for the genre, especially when fairy tale retellings and stories grounded in folklore are all the rage at the moment, with so many recent book releases that feel thematically and narratively similar. It’s also not my favorite book by Novik, and incidentally, I preferred Uprooted a lot more. Truly, I wish I had loved this one just as much, but I simply couldn’t get over some of my frustrations with the slower, more tedious, and bloated parts. Still a very good read, however, and I encourage you to pick this one up if you are a fan of the author or imaginative retellings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10137001848073676143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2529023365" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2529023365" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2529023365?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2018">y-out2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=elle-recs-list">elle-recs-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=identity">identity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2019">z-faves2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=trope-subversion">trope-subversion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-specfic">sff-specfic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2529023365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15126597949438702185"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>But the world I wanted wasn't the world I lived in, and if I would do nothing until I could repair every terrible thing at once, I would do nothing forever.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Spinning Silver</i> is a masterful tapestry of interwoven stories. Containing some of the best lady protagonists of recent fantasy literature, a fantastic narrative around cultural Jewishness, and such diverse fairy tales inspirations as Rumplestiltskin, Hansel & Gretel, A Thousand And One Arabian Nights, and Hades & Persephone, this </span>
  <span id="freeText15126597949438702185" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>But the world I wanted wasn't the world I lived in, and if I would do nothing until I could repair every terrible thing at once, I would do nothing forever.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><i>Spinning Silver</i> is a masterful tapestry of interwoven stories. Containing some of the best lady protagonists of recent fantasy literature, a fantastic narrative around cultural Jewishness, and such diverse fairy tales inspirations as Rumplestiltskin, Hansel &amp; Gretel, A Thousand And One Arabian Nights, and Hades &amp; Persephone, this book was an <i>absolute</i> masterpiece and one of my faves of the year. <br /><br />This book takes in place in many, many points of view: <br />→Miryem Mandelstam – a moneylender’s daughter who takes over the job from her father. Determined, somewhat ambitious, fiercely loving towards her family, and honestly one of the most iconic characters ever. <br />→Wanda Vitkus – the eldest sister of her family, fiercely protective of her brothers Sergey and Stepon. Her friendship with Miryem made me so emo. <br />→Irina – the daughter of a minor lord, occasionally manipulative, trying to save herself and find freedom from her father all in one. <br />→Stepon Vitkus – the youngest Vitkus, naive but loving. <br />→Margreta – Irina’s caretaker, deeply caring and quietly strong. <br />→The Starek King – definition of an ambiguous character. <br />→Prince Mirnatius – possibly possessed, definitely ambiguous. <br /><br />Oh, god, so what do I say about this novel. This is a hard one to talk about because <b>
  <i>every story is so tightly and cleverly woven</i>
</b>. The initial slow buildup of characters first struck me as a bit overlong, but over the course of the novel I came to appreciate how well <i>built</i> it all is. <b>Every payoff of this novel feels so excellently payed off.</b> Foreshadowing comes to perfect fruition; plot twists make you gasp at how obvious they seem in hindsight. It’s a tightly wound 450 pages that <b>kept me on the edge of my seat, even when the plot itself slowed down</b>. <br /><br />The other aspect, of course, is the <b>meta-narrative around identity</b>. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>But it was all the same choice, every time. The choice between the one death and all the little ones.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Judaism, historically, was often seen as something devilish, a religion of moneylenders who cheat others of their money. Historically, Jewish people were really only moneylenders because 1) many Christian sects felt it went against their religion and because 2) they often quite literally were not allowed into other trades: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Jews#Western_and_Christian_antisemitism" rel="nofollow noopener">you can read more about this here</a>.<br />This book uses Jewish identity as a positive identity, an identity belonging to the outsider and yet a positive one nonetheless. <b>It is through identity, both within the context of society and as <i>people</i>, that these characters must find strength.</b><br /><br />And the thing is, women in this book do fall in love and care for male characters. But the narrative always puts their agency, growth and development first. <b>Miryem, Wanda, and Irina all exist on their own, independent of men, even in points where men attempt to steal their story.</b> <i>Spinning Silver</i> is, in itself, <b>a meta-narrative about storytelling, about the distances we go to change the stories of others.</b> Rumpelstiltskin is a bastardized tale meant to villainize Jewish people; some fairy tales we hear at night don't get it right.<br /><br />It is here that I will go into a brief spoiler section and discuss three elements of this book that I want to talk about but don't want to spoil y'all for.<br /><b>on jewish identity as a positive gift</b>: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There’s this moment from this book that I can’t stop thinking about, in which Shofer, Flek, and Tsop, Miryem’s maidservants help her in her quest to turn the three storerooms to gold, knowing that if they fail they will themselves die. One of these three has a daughter, a daughter with no name. As a sign of their love for Miryem, she asks her to name her daughter. Miryem gives her the name Rebekah, a Jewish name, specifically as a sign of her respect for the three and for the child’s honor. Jewish cultural identity as a positive gift. I honestly don’t know why this made me cry but it made me cry really hard. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><b>on a <i>really</i> well-planted twist</b>: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I should have seen Mirnatius not having sold his soul coming!! I should have!! And I only figured it out... about twenty pages before it was revealed? I absolutely love this kind of plot reveal, the kind that adds another layer to an existing narrative and is so wonderfully set up for the audience to go "oh shit, I should have guessed that". It's possible to figure out but not obvious, and keeps its weight whether guessed or not. God bless. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><b>on the two romances-sort-of</b>: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I love that both of the romances in this book are necessary for satisfying-conclusion reasons but are still treated with a deft hand. I <i>also</i> love that both romances in this book are built off men deciding they respect women who are far more powerful and good at everything than they are. Wanda is a lesbian. Also I actually liked Irina and Mirnatius... so much? That scene where they were faking marital sex... honestly one of the funniest things I've read this year. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><b>on my shrine to the final line</b>: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />“And on the wedding contract, before me and my parents and the rabbi, and Wanda and Sergey for our witnesses, in silver ink he signed his name.<br />But I won't ever tell you what it is.”<br />The last line of this book is the single most delightful line of storytelling text I've ever read. It's <i>such an obvious line</i> but when I read it I seriously wanted to drop the book from pure appreciation of how clever that was. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I also want to take a second to comment on <b>the audiobook performance being excellent.</b> I read the last 100 pages of this in physical copy because my loan was due back. But the way the audiobook narrator dropped her voice for Wanda and raised it for Stepon... academy award, literally. You could tell the difference in narrators <i>so fucking fast</i>.<br /><br />I don’t want to say a lot more about this book besides that I think you should read it if you like character development, strong women, calling out antisemitism within narrative, subversive retellings of old narratives, and several really excellent plot reveals. <b>I closed this book feeling a sense of satisfaction I doubt will be matched by any other book I read this year.</b><br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://sptfy.com/4E3o" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/c/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15126597949438702185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2672793312" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2672793312" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2672793312?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=nenia-recommends">nenia-recommends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=you-remind-me-of-the-babe">you-remind-me-of-the-babe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=faeries-and-elves">faeries-and-elves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=best-scifi-fantasy">best-scifi-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2672793312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2656654191561116238"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>I <i>loved </i>SPINNING SILVER. And it's funny, because I only felt lukewarm about her previous book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1792041060' rel='nofollow noopener'>UPROOTED</a>. Don't get me wrong - UPROOTED wasn't a <i>bad </i>book, and I still occasionally have nightmares about heart-trees, but it didn't wow me the way I expected it to based on all the preliminary reviews, either.<br/><br/><br/><br/>SPINNING SILVER reads like Naomi Novik saw my review for UPROOTED, said to herself, "Aha," and then set about to write a story that pers</span>
  <span id="freeText2656654191561116238" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>I <i>loved </i>SPINNING SILVER. And it's funny, because I only felt lukewarm about her previous book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1792041060" rel="nofollow noopener">UPROOTED</a>. Don't get me wrong - UPROOTED wasn't a <i>bad </i>book, and I still occasionally have nightmares about heart-trees, but it didn't wow me the way I expected it to based on all the preliminary reviews, either.<br><br><br><br>SPINNING SILVER reads like Naomi Novik saw my review for UPROOTED, said to herself, "Aha," and then set about to write a story that personally addressed each and every one of my complaints. UPROOTED was slow to start; SPINNING SILVER grabbed me from the beginning and wouldn't let go. UPROOTED had a very dull heroine who ends up in a very dull love story. SPINNING SILVER has a huge cast, mostly of strong female characters, and the main love story is unconventional and fraught with tension (and doesn't really come to fruition until the end). UPROOTED has a fairy-tale vibe without any clear parallels, whereas SPINNING SILVER very obviously borrows elements from <i>The Glass Mountain</i>, <i>The Snow Queen</i>, and, of course, Rumpelstiltskin. In short, SPINNING SILVER is amazing.<br><br><br><br>It's difficult to describe the story because there is so much going on, in terms of plot and in terms of the large cast of characters. The main character is really a girl named Miryem, the daughter of a Jewish moneylender who ends up taking up his mantle when he proves too soft-hearted to carry out his work. Actually, that's another thing - I loved how Novik incorporated Jewish culture into this fairytale retelling, especially since the Grimm tales really aren't so kind to Jews. One need only look at the tale, <i>Jew Among the Thorns</i>, to see the rampant antisemitism. So it was great to see the greedy money-lender stereotype turned on its head, as Miryem is portrayed as fierce and capable and willing to do anything to see her family through the cold and cruel winters.<br><br><br><br>Her ability to turn a profit makes her an enemy of most people in her village, except for a girl named Wanda who Miryem's family ends up taking in as a servant to pay off her father's debt. Wanda is the daughter of an abusive alcoholic and initially, while she sees her job only as a respite from beatings and a means of getting food into her mouth, she starts to truly love Miryem's family and appreciate Miryem's strength. Wanda has two brothers named Sergey and Stepon, who also have POVs later on in the story. They are just as abused and desperate as Wanda, but have cores of strength, as well.<br><br><br><br>Then there's the daughter of a duke named Irina, whose father buys fairy silver from Miryem, when her money-making abilities catch the eye of the local fairies, the Staryk, who only live in the cold. He uses the silver jewelry as part of his daughter's trousseau, and the magical jewelry enchants anyone who looks upon it into thinking that Irina, who also has fairy blood, is beautiful. She is married as a result to a local tsar she has known since childhood, a powerful man of fire who is possessed by a demon. He wants to devour Irina, to steal her magic, unless she can offer him something better.<br><br><br><br>One of the things I loved about SPINNING SILVER is the interconnectedness and the focus on relationships. All the disparate storylines connect, sometimes in surprising ways, and it was so satisfying as a reader to see everything neatly come together. I also really appreciated how fleshed-out each character was, even the villains (who aren't as villainous as they initially appear), and how much time Novik seemed to have spent developing each character to be their own person. The ways that they interact with one another are so nuanced, platonic and romantic relationships both handled just as lovingly (which isn't always the case). And all the women characters are <i>so </i>strong.<br><br><br><br>It isn't often that I find a book that is basically perfect, which is why I tend to be somewhat stingy with my five-star ratings. But SPINNING SILVER is that book, and it deserves each one of those stars. I didn't think this book could possibly have a happy ending, but Novik surprised me there, too.<br><br><br><br>5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="2656654191561116238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2376246488" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2376246488" />
    <a title="Lucy Langford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford"><img alt="Lucy Langford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518091381p2/74034800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2376246488?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Langford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Langford" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford">Lucy Langford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781509899043" href="/book/show/42941939-spinning-silver">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2376246488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16204349091193002957">4.5****<br/><br/><i>“So the fairy silver brought you a monster of fire for a husband, and me a monster of ice. We should put them in a room together and let them make us both widows.”</i><br/><br/>While the blurb focuses on the plot of two women, I would go further to say that this book focused on three women whose stories and lives interlace. <br/><br/>Miryem is tough and clever (and my favourite), the daughter of a moneylender but lives in poverty as her father's too-kind heart doesn't go out to collect the money from the indebte</span>
  <span id="freeText16204349091193002957" style="display:none">4.5****<br /><br /><i>“So the fairy silver brought you a monster of fire for a husband, and me a monster of ice. We should put them in a room together and let them make us both widows.”</i><br /><br />While the blurb focuses on the plot of two women, I would go further to say that this book focused on three women whose stories and lives interlace. <br /><br />Miryem is tough and clever (and my favourite), the daughter of a moneylender but lives in poverty as her father's too-kind heart doesn't go out to collect the money from the indebted villagers. To pick her family up and out of poverty, Miryem toughens up and takes up her fathers work. Soon she travels to local towns creating more profit and when the rumour of her ability to turn silver to gold reaches the Strayk King's ears; a fairy king of winter and the people of his land, he sets her an almost impossible task- and if she fails this challenge she dies. However, if she triumphs her fate will completely change and death may be more preferable.<br /><br />Irina's father schemes and wants to marry her to the tsar. While first Irina is described as plain and rather unappealing to the tsar, the unexpected betrothel to him comes as a surprise. However, Irina soon finds that the tsar contains a terrible secret within himself, which threatens both mortals and those of the winter alike.<br /><br />Wanda is kind-hearted, a hard worker and a gentle soul. Unfortunately, she lives in poverty trying to provide for her family and living with a drunk, abusive father. To me Wanda was the Brienne of Tarth of this novel and would go to any lengths to protect those that she loves and cares about. I loved her amazement and wonder at words and numbers, providing her with a source of awe and magic.<br /><br />All three women are torn between deadly choices and all embark on their own quests. These quests encompass sacrifice, love, family and power. <br /><br />The descriptions of winter and coldness reminded me of the writing in "The Winternight Trilogy" by Katherine Arden. The writing was strongly atmospheric and descriptive that you could imagine the icy conditions of the Staryk mountain, the villages and the forests.<br /><br />I loved the development and descriptions of all three main female characters. While different in characteristics and looks, all three are described as rather plain in looks. This was great for me as I find a lot of books will suddenly introduce absolutely stunning women which can make it hard to relate to. Also by making them plain the author attributes their biggest characteristics to their decisions and actions. <br /><br />My favourite character was Miryem and I loved her interactions with the Staryk King- their discontent and hate for each other was entertaining, while also providing the reader with witty remarks.<br /><br />If you couldn't tell-I loved this. 💙<br />It was 2am when I finished the book as I just could not put it down! It is an immersive and stunning read, with fascinating female leads taking control of their lives.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16204349091193002957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2338219911" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2338219911" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2338219911?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well">he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bubbling-under-5-stars">bubbling-under-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=girl-squad">girl-squad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2338219911" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4288188127041081785"><b>4.25 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“The real story isn’t half as pretty as the one you’ve heard.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>Do you know how long I’ve waited for a Rumpelstiltskin retelling? </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547048699ra/26892058.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It is the one fairy tale where the villain doesn’t deserve his comeuppance. He made a bargain with the miller’s daughter and she weaseled out of it. We don’t know for certain what he was going to do with that kid! Sure, he was dancing in front of a cauldron, but that evidence is circumstantial. He could have fed fine cuts of meat, sent it to the finest sch</span>
  <span id="freeText4288188127041081785" style="display:none"><b>4.25 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“The real story isn’t half as pretty as the one you’ve heard.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Do you know how long I’ve waited for a Rumpelstiltskin retelling? </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547048699ra/26892058.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It is the one fairy tale where the villain doesn’t deserve his comeuppance. He made a bargain with the miller’s daughter and she weaseled out of it. We don’t know for certain what he was going to do with that kid! Sure, he was dancing in front of a cauldron, but that evidence is circumstantial. He could have fed fine cuts of meat, sent it to the finest schools, and nurtured it like Kaz with his grudges. <br><br>But back to the retelling. Spinning Silver doesn’t follow the original narrative to the letter. The <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36381037.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_" title="Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener"> Lunar Chronicles</a> did; it more or less follows the exact plot of the related fairy tale if you read closely. It's more subtle in Spinning Silver. There are events and symbols I can point to and go, “Ah-ha, I recognize you.” The three impossible gold-spinning tasks the Staryk King gives Mireyem, for instance, or the idea of bargains. <br><br>It was a fascinating choice to make Mireyem Jewish because of the frequent association of Jews to wealth, but a choice that works very well. It adds to the symbolic undertone of the novel. A girl who can breed pennies to wealth, spin silver to gold.<br><br><b>Overwhelmingly, undoubtedly though, this is a story about sisterhood.</b> Three women to be exact: Mireyem, Wanda, and Irina. Mireyem originally asks Wanda to work at her home to pay off her father’s debt. Little does she know it’s a blessing in disguise because Wanda’s father is abusive and just wants to marry her off at the best price. The girls soon develop a bond. Meanwhile, in another part of the country, Irina is married to the tsar who is widely rumored to be allied with a demon. Their lives eventually intersect, and it’s a joy to read. They don’t always agree with each other—which I love—but their bonds are forged by camaraderie and mutual respect. <br><br>After the home run Novik scored with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a>, I'd happily read any retelling she comes up with next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4288188127041081785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2906294110" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2906294110" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2906294110?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fairy-tale-retellings">fairy-tale-retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2906294110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13375806914827354816">This is a whole different beast from most fairytale retellings I read. Different even from the author’s previously released magnificent tale—Uprooted. Uprooted, from what I recall, was thoroughly enchanting and exquisitely written. Spinning Silver is not quite like that. It is not a love story first and foremost—it is a story of survival. It is very feminist with three central female protagonists who experience, learn and grow. The writing is in no way purple-y. The author's main concern is not </span>
  <span id="freeText13375806914827354816" style="display:none">This is a whole different beast from most fairytale retellings I read. Different even from the author’s previously released magnificent tale—Uprooted. Uprooted, from what I recall, was thoroughly enchanting and exquisitely written. Spinning Silver is not quite like that. It is not a love story first and foremost—it is a story of survival. It is very feminist with three central female protagonists who experience, learn and grow. The writing is in no way purple-y. The author's main concern is not to wow us with long beautiful descriptions of what are ultimately meaningless things and she doesn’t embellish what is meant to be raw and impactful.<br /><br />In other words, it is not a beautiful and perfect tale from beginning to end; it is a hard tale. There is struggle, violence, unfairness, mischief and sadness. Uprooted was more beautiful and romantic and exciting but it wasn’t necessarily better. It simply depends on what you need right now. I needed to read a meaningful fantasy and while fairytales are, well, fairytales and so hardly important to my daily life, this tale actually mattered to me very much. I was interested in the fate of all characters and despite being a slow story, I did not lose interest at any point. Whether the author decided to do this to spice up the story or make us feel connected to more characters than the three main ones, I do not know, but I appreciated the POVs from selected secondary characters also. I just wish the shift between POVs were clearer. <br /><br />The best time to read this story is during summer, truly, because this is a cold fantasy world with cold magic and cold villains that will simply make you forget how hot it is outside. It is indeed a retelling of Rumpelstiltskin and a very original one at that. This should come as no surprise since Uprooted was a gem also. And I know I said that it’s not a ‘‘beautiful’’ tale, but I meant in the traditional sense because it is absolutely fantastic. I am in awe. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13375806914827354816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2466667005" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2466667005" />
    <a title="Natasha Polis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19208239-natasha-polis"><img alt="Natasha Polis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445474659p2/19208239.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2466667005?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasha Polis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasha Polis" href="/user/show/19208239-natasha-polis">Natasha Polis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2466667005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8234047591946087305">Wished it to be more romantic since it is an adult fantasy novel. Had to get the audiobook to finish it, but still very enjoyable as Naomi really knows how to create a sinister fairytale esque world. The main character is Jewish and her religion and customs is brought up many times which is something I greatly appreciated as it shows how your heritage and morals drives a person. Very smart and beautiful story, just wished for more elaboration on the romantic relationships.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2993735196" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2993735196" />
    <a title="Kevin Kuhn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59568642-kevin-kuhn"><img alt="Kevin Kuhn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508679965p2/59568642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2993735196?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin Kuhn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin Kuhn" href="/user/show/59568642-kevin-kuhn">Kevin Kuhn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fantasy Fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59568642-kevin-kuhn?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2993735196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6526716636431913556">Naomi Novik published this book in 2018 and it won the 2019 Locus Award for Best Fantasy Novel. It was also nominated for 2019 Hugo Award for Best Novel. To me it is three things; a retelling of Rumpelstiltskin, a mythic fable exploring mankind’s battle with winter, and the story of the powerless finding hope, strength and ultimately the power to overcome evil and subjugation. It is the third aspect that gave me the most enjoyment. I’m somehow fascinated with stories that deal with the underdog,</span>
  <span id="freeText6526716636431913556" style="display:none">Naomi Novik published this book in 2018 and it won the 2019 Locus Award for Best Fantasy Novel. It was also nominated for 2019 Hugo Award for Best Novel. To me it is three things; a retelling of Rumpelstiltskin, a mythic fable exploring mankind’s battle with winter, and the story of the powerless finding hope, strength and ultimately the power to overcome evil and subjugation. It is the third aspect that gave me the most enjoyment. I’m somehow fascinated with stories that deal with the underdog, whether it’s the Hobbits in Lord of the Rings, or Gandhi verses the British Empire. The ability of the downtrodden’s ability to find influence especially through non-violence, never fails to spark enthusiasm and intrigue for me.<br /><br />Honestly, this was not a quick read for me, in fact at many points, I found it to be laborious. But I never wanted to give up, I somehow knew that the ending would be satisfying, and it was. Novik tells the tale from many character perspectives and this is jarring at first. In fact, she occasionally retells a scene, from an alternate perspective, which I found unusual and it caused me to step out of the story momentarily to contemplate the technique. However, after a while, I accepted this, and it became a game to me, to see how quickly I could deduce which character’s point of view was taken in a new section. As a reader, I do like to work a little! <br /><br />The plot follows largely follows three women, all who’s dismal future is laid out in front of them, and all who dare to fight against that future. Their stories are entwined in excellent ways. The story also weaves components of the Rumpelstiltskin myth and the parable of human’s struggle against winter. Novak’s prose feels like a classic fairy tale without feeling old-fashioned or dated. <br /><br />A slower paced, but enjoyable fable with great fantasy worldbuilding, intertwined themes and characters, and a strong and satisfying ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6526716636431913556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2437449884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2437449884" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2437449884?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2018-shelf">2018-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2437449884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer163215667673643586">A lot of these retellings of old myths and fairy tales are hit or miss with me, but I come to you today to tell you that this was not a miss. :) Indeed, nothing was amiss.<br/><br/>The combination of several different old fairy tales and the new-norm for Russian-style fantasy hit all the right buttons for me. There was nothing simple about this tale even though we learn, slowly, that the world is not all about hard poverty and abuse and little towns and harsh Czars. That jews aren't necessarily cracked up</span>
  <span id="freeText163215667673643586" style="display:none">A lot of these retellings of old myths and fairy tales are hit or miss with me, but I come to you today to tell you that this was not a miss. :) Indeed, nothing was amiss.<br /><br />The combination of several different old fairy tales and the new-norm for Russian-style fantasy hit all the right buttons for me. There was nothing simple about this tale even though we learn, slowly, that the world is not all about hard poverty and abuse and little towns and harsh Czars. That jews aren't necessarily cracked up to fit their stereotypes. <br /><br />But one thing is true. The Winter King can be cruel and harsh, the stakes are often hidden but quite vast, and simple, if powerful, magics are never enough when a Great Working is desperately needed.<br /><br />At least two big stories are interwoven here, between a seamstress who marries the Czar and the moneylender's daughter who gets carried away by the Winter King. No spoilers, but there's a ton of discoveries to be had in each realm and the clash between them is something quite wonderful and amazing, even for someone who has read a ton of fantasy.<br /><br />I can honestly say that Novik outdid herself here. This is a quality myth, newly-owned and told fresh. Do I like it better than Uprooted?<br /><br />Yes.<br /><br />I may have liked the other one better for its subject matter, but this one had a much tighter plot and a more satisfying end. More than this will be getting into deep spoiler territory.<br /><br />Suffice to say, I loved it. :)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="163215667673643586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2219664947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2219664947" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2219664947?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=cool-creatures">cool-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fae-ness">fae-ness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bb-b-2018">bb-b-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2219664947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17909779899633526091">Uprooted was one of my favorite reads of 2016, so I was beyond thrilled that Naomi Novik was again going to give us a new fairytale. Spinning Silver has some roots in Rumpelstiltskin but don’t think that means you know how this story is going to go because even though you might see a resemblance this is a brand new fairytale.<br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“A power claimed and challenged and thrice carried out is true”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>The world for this has foundations from the Jewish culture, blended into a world with subtle magic</span>
  <span id="freeText17909779899633526091" style="display:none">Uprooted was one of my favorite reads of 2016, so I was beyond thrilled that Naomi Novik was again going to give us a new fairytale. Spinning Silver has some roots in Rumpelstiltskin but don’t think that means you know how this story is going to go because even though you might see a resemblance this is a brand new fairytale.<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“A power claimed and challenged and thrice carried out is true”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>The world for this has foundations from the Jewish culture, blended into a world with subtle magics and a people from a mystical icy realm who are both mysterious and dangerous. I really enjoyed how Novik blended all of these parts together to give us an entirely new story that feels like it is old and a classic fairytale already.<br>Spinning Silver is a multiple PoV fantasy that follows a few characters as their stories and the world around them grows. Miryem is the daughter of the worst money collector in history. She comes from a very loving home but there is never enough because her father is horrible at collecting from the people who owe. Miryem takes it upon herself to take over the business with a cool detachment that makes her fantastic and collecting coin. So good in fact she catches the eye of the Staryk King who has use for a peasant girl that can turn silver into gold. ← <i>see what she did there</i><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“But I had not known that I was strong enough to do any of those things until they were over and I had done them. I had to do the work first, not knowing.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Wanda, comes from an impoverished farm and has never really known kindness. Her father is a drunk and a brute and all she has ever known is finding a way to just get by. You’d think being sent to work for the moneylender to pay off her father’s debts would be the worst thing to happen to her, but it ends up being the best thing to help her and for her to later help others.<br><br>Lastly is Irena, a Dukes daughter with some Staryk blood in her. She has a treacherous path to take as she has caught the eye of a demon. With her wits about her and help from some unlikely friends she just might keep herself out of the demon’s hands.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Best Thing</u>
</b> about this new/old fairytale is that the women in it seemed real. None of them were overly beautiful or fetching, but each had a special quality either with their smarts, ingenuity or just strength of will that made them special. I loved that as we grow to know the characters they become three dimensional and you fall in love with them as other characters in the story discover their worth.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Worst Thing For Me</u>
</b> was the very reduced romance aspect of this. There is a little and it is enough to keep me interested and hopeful but in the end I would have enjoyed just a smidge more. But there is some so it is a minor thing. <br><br>If you like Russian Folklore, Fairytales or just a good Fantasy with a lot of world building aspects to it then Spinning Silver might be just what you need.<br><br><b>Audio Note</b>: While I liked the audio of this quite a bit when the narrator changed PoVs inside the chapters it was sometime very hard to tell especially in the beginning. I did like how her accent added to the overall feel of the story though.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514037790i/24745573._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="17909779899633526091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_36621586'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36621586-the-winter-of-the-witch"><img alt="The Winter of the Witch (Winternight Trilogy, #3)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1517001188l/36621586._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eGfe8CyBJQHbSxlHKCzx5sfJchqSQUI8rPdVVRrN3O0d6LrnfAQ0rVBB974cTDtUACNVRBS6ZigqfX9UgTB2YA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/Z9q7Wa+pNHsUQ/feaU0WrubTjDsdXzxAh4ZQAX+Pj6YEA76Nju1fWdb4SZNxf7ofHFpbmqOWOWElDNBngOUsw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8730.Naomi_Novik">About Naomi Novik</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8730.Naomi_Novik"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1206646770p3/8730.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/8730.Naomi_Novik">Naomi Novik
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
18,834
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9734240800336044543">An avid reader of fantasy literature since age six, when she first made her way through The Lord of the Rings, Naomi Novik is also a history buff with a particular interest in the Napoleonic era and a fondness for the work of Patrick O’Brian and Jane Austen. She studied English literature at Brown University, and did graduate work in computer science at Columbia University before leaving to partic</span>
  <span id="freeText9734240800336044543" style="display:none">An avid reader of fantasy literature since age six, when she first made her way through The Lord of the Rings, Naomi Novik is also a history buff with a particular interest in the Napoleonic era and a fondness for the work of Patrick O’Brian and Jane Austen. She studied English literature at Brown University, and did graduate work in computer science at Columbia University before leaving to participate in the design and development of the computer game Neverwinter Nights: Shadow of Undrentide. Over the course of a brief winter sojourn spent working on the game in Edmonton, Canada (accompanied by a truly alarming coat that now lives brooding in the depths of her closet), she realized she preferred writing to programming, and on returning to New York, decided to try her hand at novels.<br /><br />Naomi lives in New York City with her husband and six computers. Her website is at naominovik.com</span>
  <a data-text-id="9734240800336044543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
